## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / constitutive modeling in materials science (thermo-mechanical stress–strain behavior)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which points to constitutive laws for elasticity/plasticity with thermal expansion and thermal softening. Typical relationships include elastic modulus and yield/flow stress depending on T, plus nonlinear hardening with epsilon.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linearized): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (E varies approximately linearly with T over a limited range)
- Thermoelastic with thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress from mechanical strain after subtracting thermal expansion strain)
- Nonlinear (polynomial) elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (finite-strain/nonlinear elastic response)
- Hyperelastic-type saturation (strain stiffening/softening): sigma = c0 * (exp(c1 * epsilon) - 1) (rapid stiffening with strain)
- Hollomon power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic flow curve approximation beyond yield)
- Ludwik hardening (offset strain): sigma = c0 + c1 * (epsilon + c2)**c3 (yield + power-law hardening with strain offset)
- Ramberg–Osgood (implicit elastic+plastic form, rearranged): epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * sigma**c2 (captures elastic compliance plus nonlinear plastic strain; used when fitting sigma–epsilon curves)
- Voce hardening (saturating flow stress): sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (hardening toward a saturation stress)
- Thermal softening of flow stress (multiplicative): sigma = (c0 * epsilon**c1) * exp(-c2 * T) (strength decreases with increasing temperature)
- Johnson–Cook-type without strain-rate term: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T + c5 * T**2) (empirical hardening times thermal softening factor; polynomial-in-T variant)
- Coupled thermo-mechanical nonlinearity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2 * exp(-c3 * T) (elastic part with E(T) plus temperature-softened nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Initial linear slope in sigma vs epsilon at fixed T suggests an elastic modulus term E(T) multiplying epsilon (sigma ≈ E(T)*epsilon).
- A horizontal shift of the sigma–epsilon curve with T is often captured by subtracting a thermal strain term proportional to (T - T0) inside (epsilon - alpha*(T-T0)).
- If higher T reduces stresses roughly proportionally across strains, multiplicative thermal softening factors (e.g., exp(-c*T) or low-order polynomials in T) are common.
- If sigma approaches a limiting value as epsilon increases, use saturating hardening structures like (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or rational saturations.
- If sigma increases slowly at small epsilon and accelerates later (or vice versa), consider exponential-in-epsilon or higher-order polynomial elasticity terms.
- Approximately straight lines on log(sigma) vs log(epsilon) plots indicate power-law hardening sigma ~ epsilon**n.
- If temperature changes the curvature (not just scale), include cross terms like epsilon**p * T**q or epsilon**p * exp(-c*T).
- If near T ranges show nearly linear dependence, approximate E(T) or yield(T) with affine forms (c0 + c1*T) before trying more complex T-dependence.

**GT expression:**
`-c0*(T - c1) + epsilon**c2 * c3 * (T - c4)`

where c1 = c4 = 352.1579..., c0 = 0.5449..., c2 = 0.6261..., c3 = 1.5180...

This has the structure: `A*T + B + C*T*epsilon**c2 + D*epsilon**c2`

where A = -c0, B = c0*c1, C = c3, D = -c3*c4

The key basis functions are: **T**, **1** (constant), **T*epsilon^c2**, **epsilon^c2**

Now let me check each candidate. Since epsilon ≥ 0 (domain constraint), |epsilon| = epsilon, and epsilon**c2 = |epsilon|**c2.

I'll focus on candidates that have the right structure: terms involving T, constant, T*epsilon^p, and epsilon^p.

**Candidates 59, 62, 63, 6, 60, 61** look most promising as they contain T*epsilon^c terms.

**Candidate 59:** `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + T*c2*|epsilon|^c3 + c4*epsilon + c5*|epsilon|^c3 + c6`
= T*(c0*epsilon + c1 + c2*epsilon^c3) + c4*epsilon + c5*epsilon^c3 + c6

This has T*epsilon term (linear in epsilon) which GT doesn't have. We can set c0=0 to eliminate it, giving: T*c1 + T*c2*epsilon^c3 + c4*epsilon + c5*epsilon^c3 + c6. But this still has c4*epsilon which GT doesn't have. Set c4=0: T*c1 + T*c2*epsilon^c3 + c5*epsilon^c3 + c6. This matches! (A=c1, C=c2, D=c5, B=c6)

**Candidate 59 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 62:** `T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon**c2 + c3 + c4*epsilon + c5*epsilon**c2`
Set c4=0: T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon^c2 + c3 + c5*epsilon^c2. This matches GT perfectly!

**Candidate 62 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 63:** `T*c0 + T*c1*|epsilon|^c2 + c3*epsilon + c4*|epsilon|^c2 + c5`
Set c3=0: T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon^c2 + c4*epsilon^c2 + c5. Matches!

**Candidate 63 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 6:** `T*c0 + T*c1*|epsilon|^c2 + c3*epsilon + c4*|epsilon|^c2 + c5 + c6*|epsilon|^c7`
Set c3=0, c6=0: matches. 

**Candidate 6 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 60:** Has log term but can set c6=0. Remaining: T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon^c2 + c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon^c2 + c5. Set c3=0: matches.
**Candidate 60 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 61:** Has sqrt term, set c6=0: same as 60 without log. Matches with c3=0.
**Candidate 61 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 55, 57, 58:** Let me check 55: has T²*c0 term - set c0=0. Then T*c1 + T*c2*|eps|^c3 + c4*eps + c5*|eps|^c3 + c6 + c7*|eps|^c8. Set c4=0, c7=0: matches.
**Candidate 55 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 57:** T²*c0 + T²*c1*|eps|^c2 + ... Set c0=0,c1=0: T*c3*eps + T*c4 + T*c5*|eps|^c2 + c6*eps + c7*|eps|^c2 + c8. Set c3=0, c6=0: matches.
**Candidate 57 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 58:** Has log(T*c7+1) - cannot match T. Set c6=0 makes log disappear: T*c0 + T*c1*|eps|^c2 + c3*eps + c4*|eps|^c2 + c5. Set c3=0: matches.
**Candidate 58 verdict: [MATCH]**
